[2023-09-02 12:43:13] 614946962139250711: It worked for me in my local hugging face. Kind of confusing the way you use it:
```
bark_text_prompt = "Of all the things in the I world I like text prompts the most. I like them so much I want to generate them."
bark_semantic_input = processor(bark_text_prompt, voice_preset="lex.npz").to(device) # this it ehs same directory as the script I'm running
bark_semantic_output = model.semantic.generate(
    **bark_semantic_input,
    do_sample=True,
    # history_prompt=history_prompt, # this is not passed 
    semantic_generation_config=semantic_generation_config,
)
```

[2023-09-03 18:28:42] 238071088666509312: There are a few factors that determine the cash costs of running an AI generation website:

    Compute costs: AI models like GPT-3 require significant GPU/TPU computing power to generate text, which can be expensive if using cloud services. Renting from cloud providers like AWS, GCP, or Azure can easily cost thousands of dollars per month depending on usage.
    Data storage: Storing all the text, audio, video, etc. that AI models are trained on requires lots of data storage, which also costs money with cloud providers. This can cost hundreds to thousands per month.
    Traffic costs: The more users and requests, the higher the compute, bandwidth, and data costs. Popular AI sites can rack up big bills fast if traffic scales up. Caching and optimization helps reduce this.
    Staffing: Dedicated engineering staff are needed to build, deploy, and maintain AI systems, backend, APIs, frontends, etc. Salary and benefits for staff can be a significant recurring cost.
    Model costs: Licensing large pre-trained models like GPT-3 from companies like Anthropic, Cohere, etc. costs money based on usage. Can be thousands+ per month.
    Development costs: Initial development and continued improvements require investment. Can be tens to hundreds of thousands in upfront costs.

So in summary, monthly costs for a moderately popular AI site with dedicated infrastructure could easily total $10k-$100k+ per month, with high scaling costs for traffic. Reducing compute, minimizing wasted requests, controlling model usage, and optimizing infrastructure are key to controlling long-term costs.

[2023-09-08 04:54:18] 614946962139250711: **How do you make a song longer than 30s in Chirp? **
**The way to make long songs is to combine the outputs from 30s Chirp clips to make one longer song clip.** 

🐣 **->** 🎵
🐣**+** ⏩ **+** ⏩ **+** ❤️ **->**  🎶🎶

I might repost this start of every night, because it's often the first question I get from people joining the server trying Chirp for the first time:

1. If you click the arrow button ⏩ on one clip, you create another clip that starts at the end of the that clip. **⏩1** is the left audio clip. **⏩2** is the right audio clip.
2. You will get a new Chirp popup form to put the lyrics and prompt for the next section. If you leave the genre field blank it will generally match the music style and genre of the clip you are continuing from, however, it can very interesting to *change * the genre and Chirp will try and smoothly transition from one style to another. You can can also try copying and pasting your old genre and then slowly morphing the style a little in each follow-up clip by changing a word or two each time.
3. For any clip you can always click the heart ❤️ button. If you click this on a song clip that is a continue of another song section, the bot will send you a longer song that is all the sections combined into once. So if it's the second clip, you get two sections. If it's the 10th clip, it's 10 seconds put together. There is no charge for clicking ❤️ so use it as much as you want on any of your outputs.

You can continue from the same clip multiple times. So if your third section didn't come out right, go back to clip 2 and click the ⏩  again. Or go back to clip 1 and make a new clip 2, etc. 

You can continue not just from your own songs, but from any song in the public channels, and likewise other people can continue from your songs. So listen to other people's songs so you can find cool clips to try adding onto. If you prefer not to have other people use your songs, you can DM the Suno chirp Bot instead and they will stay private.

[2023-09-08 20:37:24] 1024867715917303861: Working on a ChatGPT prompt to better help design the layout structure for the "Describe the style of music" Section of the SUNO Chirp Bot. This doesn't include anything regarding the vocal portion and is currently being tested but the more the merrier. What I've been doing is putting this prompt into ChatGPT and it will ask you for a reference genre/song/etc, Once you give it that it should provide a list of segments (numerically listed) for a user to build a song with. This applies solely for the use of continuances.  Segment 1 would be where you start, and then 2, and so on. Again this is still in early testing phase but I thought I'd share in case it gave any of you some helpful ideas. The attached picture shows you where to put the segment.
[2023-09-08 20:37:32] 1024867715917303861: ```Prompt for Single Line Song Structure Generation with Instrument and Dynamic Control

Description:
This guide aids the AI in creating single-line song structure suggestions. It emphasizes the use of specific instruments, mood, tempo, prominence, and dynamic control, all rooted in a particular song or genre.

Procedure:

Start by asking the user for their preferred song, genre, or influence.
Once the user provides their choice, immediately acknowledge it.
Use the provided information to design a brief song structure.
List the song sections numerically and separate each song part (Intro, Verse, Chorus, etc.) distinctly, using newlines.
Format song sections as: "[Genre/Influence] Section, instruments (with prominence control, dynamic control), mood/tempo".
Define prominence control to reflect the importance of the instrument in that section.
Incorporate dynamic control to specify elements such as "fade in", "fade out", "crescendo", and more.
Ensure sections transition seamlessly.
Omit end-line punctuation, but use metatags like [Verse] and [Chorus] for clarity.
Introduce non-lexical elements sparingly for a unique touch.
Interactions:

User states: "[Song/Genre/Influence]"
AI responds: "Recognizing [Song/Genre/Influence]. Here's a structured song suggestion with prominence and dynamic control: ..."

Example 1:
User: "1960s Psychedelic Rock influence"
AI: "Recognizing '1960s Psychedelic Rock' influence. Suggested structure:

[Psychedelic Rock] Intro, sitar (high prominence, fade in), mellow tempo
[Psychedelic Rock] Verse, electric guitar (medium prominence) and drums (medium prominence), vocals (high prominence), dreamy mood
..."
Example 2:
User: "Blues genre"
AI: "Recognizing Blues. Suggested structure:

[Blues] Intro, solo harmonica (high prominence, crescendo), somber tone
[Blues] Verse, slide electric guitar (medium prominence), drums (low prominence, fade in), even rhythm
..."
Interaction Guide:

The AI begins by inquiring about your musical preference.
Respond by naming a song, selecting a genre, or sharing a musical influence.
The AI will then present a concise song structure with prominence and dynamic nuances, listed numerically.
To tailor the structure or for specific requirements, provide further details or ask for modifications.
Kick off the process by sharing a song, genre, or musical influence, and the AI will design a song structure keeping prominence and dynamic elements at the forefront.
This revised guide captures dynamic intricacies while staying true to the original essence, emphasizing a numerical listing for song sections.```

[2023-09-08 21:27:53] 214966642680135683: What is the difference between these two python access methods (importing from Bark github and importing from transformers)?  Do the installation prerequisites of each place the executables and weights executables and weights on local computer?

Method #1 (import form github)
https://github.com/suno-ai/bark#-usage-in-python

from bark import SAMPLE_RATE, generate_audio, preload_models
preload_models()
generate_audio(text_prompt)

Method #2 (import from transformers)
https://github.com/suno-ai/bark#-transformers-usage

from transformers import AutoProcessor, BarkModel
processor = AutoProcessor.from_pretrained("suno/bark")
model = BarkModel.from_pretrained("suno/bark")
inputs = processor("Hello, my dog is cute", voice_preset=voice_preset)
model.generate(**inputs)

[2023-09-11 18:25:55] 1024867715917303861: It should work if you are doing the process correctly...

1. /chirp
2. Fill in genre/lyrics
3. Generate first 30 sec
4. Heart 1 or 2
5. Continuation 1 or 2 (should be the same that you hearted)
6. Fill in genre/lyrics for continuation
7. Heart 1 or 2
8. rinse and repeat.
(The result from the second heart will provide you with the combination of the first and second part)

[2023-09-13 20:26:26] 1133894577137397820: when we edit renditions does that reduce our credits? I'm having a bit of a hard time getting this app..🧐
[2023-09-13 20:34:30] 614946962139250711: Each generation of new audio uses credits. So clicking an arrow to make a new version is the same cost as making a new segment. But clicking the heart is just putting together already generated sections, so does not cost credits.
[2023-09-13 20:37:26] 1133894577137397820: Thanks! Good to know
[2023-09-13 20:39:53] 1133894577137397820: Hey Jonathan or @—DAViD—... thanks for your reply. Quick question please... what do the hearts do vs what the arrows do?
[2023-09-13 20:41:58] 614946962139250711: The arrow make a new 30s song that starts off at the end of the clip you click the arrow on. So the idea is you make your first 30s of song, then you click the arrow on one of those song clips (choose 1 or 2) and then add 30s more (with new lyrics, etc) and build up to make a longer song. The heart does two things. The first is just a 'like' to show you like that section. But also if you click the heart on a 30s song section that is not the first one (it's a section made with a continue arrow) then the Suno bot will combine all the previous sections into one long for you. Detailed instructions: https://discord.com/channels/1069381916492562582/1149508588470022164/1149742422381826048
[2023-09-13 20:42:41] 614946962139250711: **Normal Workflow**: 🐣  =  🎵

**Continuation Workflow**: 🐣  +  ⏩  +  ⏩  +  ❤️  =  🎵 🎵 🎵

[2023-09-15 02:24:20] 1132195332512559215: I want to know how to control speaking speed in bark . Does anyone know?
[2023-09-15 02:28:19] 342180697483509770: damn this tool is great

[2023-09-15 02:45:03] 1132195332512559215: I want to know how to control speaking speed in bark . Does anyone know? @mylo  @Jonathan Fly
[2023-09-15 02:59:48] 614946962139250711: A simple but still very effective way is to use very text large prompts with a voice, and re-save it, to make a faster speaker version. You can do this with an existing voice but also if you use very large prompts with a random voice, you can very easily get fast speaking voices.
[2023-09-15 03:00:46] 614946962139250711: It's usually a little trickier in reverse, but making a voice faster is pretty reliable this way.
[2023-09-15 03:09:24] 614946962139250711: For very fast, you want to literally use so much text that 9 out of 10 samples don't finish reading the text. And then you use the 1 out of 10 that DOES finish reading in 14s, as your new voice.
[2023-09-15 03:10:26] 614946962139250711: The same thing works to slow down a voice but you generally have to not just use a short prompt, but add in pausing like '...' into the text, and extra commas, etc.
[2023-09-15 03:10:26] 1132195332512559215: tks ,it's a way ,But it's not possible to make one sentence speak fast and another sentence speak slow use one speaker version.
[2023-09-15 03:11:47] 614946962139250711: Well you can switch between the voice you saved as fast and slow for each sentence, and use each one seperately. But switching mid generation of one single segment is not easy. I think there's probably some things that might work but haven't really even tested it myself, would need some kind of meta-syntax in the text prompt.
[2023-09-15 03:15:23] 1132195332512559215: Got it, thanks!
[2023-09-15 03:21:36] 1132195332512559215: if i want to understand the underlying principles, are there any recommended books or links? I'm a programmer, but not in the AI field.
[2023-09-15 03:24:52] 614946962139250711: Audio from language models is pretty new area, and a lot of this is somewhat bark-specific, but the Bark Suno code is quite readable. And a lot of concepts that apply to language models like llama and GPT have analogs or some related ideas in Bark. The main big idea is that a Bark voice and a Bark audio output is the same thing. And so a bark voice is just the preceding context in the prompt -- it's literally seconds of audio before it generates what you ask it to generate.  Just like the context in a chatgpt prompt -- Bark is just continuing the audio. And Bark will continue the audio with a voice that sounds the same as the preceding prompt. So that's why a Bark voice can just be literally single digit amount of seconds of auido.

[2023-09-15 23:09:01] 687471333403131955: Check out #🐣┃how-to-chirp

2. Type `/chirp`
3. Press Enter, and a pop-up will appear
4. Enter these lyrics

  - I'd also recommend shortening your prompt. Start with 4-8 lines.

[2023-09-16 01:20:40] 614946962139250711: With these modern AI models we can really only speculate the reasons or source for why things are the way are. It's ultimately a black box. 

But if you're using a 'random' music genre then the AI behind the scenes is typically picking a common broad music genre for each of the two samples. Country, jazz, etc. 

On the other hand, if you *clear * out the genre field (remove the word random and make it blank) then the AI will be a bit different and sort of match the lyrics against the music style that they look like (this is how the old Chirp always worked, if you were around 2+ weeks ago.)

[2023-09-16 23:49:22] 614946962139250711: The song lengths are the same between free and paid, they both make longer songs by assembling smaller pieces together. This is not always musically consistent/coherent as the pieces come together to form long songs -- especially 6 minutes, that's probably too long. So it's hard to, for example, return to a chorus later in a song and have it sung exactly the same way. As the AI gets better, this should get better, but at least for now it's a bit tricky.

It's also not possible to have fine-grained control over specific voices in the current version. *However...* you might be able to pull something off with persistence and some luck, by using the continue feature creatively. If you find a good starting song segment with a clear voice, as you continue that song segment, you can prompt with different lyrics and styles. The voice isn't always consistent but you can usually get it to be somewhat consistent at least over just a few segments. So you could in theory keep going back to your base starting voice segment and branching out in different paths to make different songs, using the same singer. Overall it's probably going to be a bit messy and require a lot of trial and error (and credits, alas) but might be able to do something like what you want.
[2023-09-16 23:53:06] 614946962139250711: If you also used traditional audio editing to blend segments, you could probably do a lot as well. For example by reusing the chorus through editing in post, instead of direct via the AI, etc.

[2023-09-17 18:50:27] 320937520378675201: @Jonathan Fly processing / group by sentence & words seem to work well for books. In terms of generating mp3, I think these would be useful options:
1. Output size:
    a. By N segments (i.e. generate an MP3 for every N segments; current "save every NPZ" option is a special case of generating by one segment)
    b. By N seconds (i.e. generate an MP3 per group of segments that correspond to approximately N seconds total)
2. Output filename: Option to specify regex or a formatted string with variables of segment_number, date, prompt, speaker.
3. Option to disable generating final output that includes all segments (since this could be too large)
4. Option to resume at segment N (i.e. after splitting segments, start at segment N rather than first segment; useful to resume on failure)

[Chorus]
{line 1}
{line 2}

and then continuation repaste that  but add a line 3 and 4, it will skip lines 1 and 2 because its already used them

[2023-09-24 11:54:47] 678242805289844739: why gpu is not being utilized for this code ```python from transformers import AutoProcessor, BarkModel
from IPython.display import Audio

processor = AutoProcessor.from_pretrained("suno/bark")
model = BarkModel.from_pretrained("suno/bark")

voice_preset = "v2/en_speaker_6"

inputs = processor("Hello, my dog is cute", voice_preset=voice_preset)

audio_array = model.generate(**inputs)
audio_array = audio_array.gpu().numpy().squeeze()

sample_rate = model.generation_config.sample_rate
Audio(audio_array, rate=sample_rate)
```
[2023-09-24 11:55:35] 678242805289844739: torch with the following code ```

import torch

if torch.cuda.is_available():
    num_gpus = torch.cuda.device_count()
    print(f"Found {num_gpus} GPU(s) available.")
    for i in range(num_gpus):
        gpu_name = torch.cuda.get_device_name(i)
        print(f"GPU {i}: {gpu_name}")
else:
    print("No GPU available. Using CPU.")``` is able to check for gpu

if you buy top up tokens, they persist as 'extra tokens' beyond the subscription, and roll-over when your month refreshes. (have not seen this happen yet, hasn't been 1 month)

[2023-09-26 21:00:07] 249386616806834177: Not that've I've seen, but I'm no expert. Maybe someone else has a better answer for that
[2023-09-26 21:05:56] 614946962139250711: You can sometimes use a prompt like that and it works, but not often. But you can try writing text in the style of an old angry woman speaking, like 3 or 4 sentence prompts where the style of that character and emotion comese through strong, and that actually can work. It's not a strict guidance though, it works in the sense that you try 5 old angry woman prompts 5 times each, listen to the samples, find a few good ones that sound perfect, and those samples are now your new voices when you want angry old woman. More in discord if search around, or maybe search my posts, but you can do the same idea with a single voice, a prompt, and saving it again. But it's more about getting one really good one and reusing it, then it is about text guidance for one generation.

[2023-09-30 23:31:44] 1024867715917303861: Also to answer your question regarding placement, text inputted into the “genre” section do not require brackets. Any suggested instruction in the lyric section will require brackets. I’ve seen users do both e.g. Rock Intro (in the genre section) and [Intro] in the lyrical section. I would play around and see which gives you the best results. Hoping when others see this, they will chime in on what they’ve learned and what works best with them
